"Variables:\nDebby's candy = 32 pieces\nSister's candy = 42 pieces\nTotal candy = 32 + 42 = 74 pieces\nCandy eaten on the first night = 35 pieces\n\nPlan:\n1. Find the total candy they have.\n2. Subtract the candy eaten on the first night from the total candy to find out how many pieces they have left.\n\nCalculation:\nTotal candy = 32 + 42 = 74 pieces\nCandy left after the first night = 74 - 35 = 39 pieces\n\nAnswer:\nThey have 39 pieces of candy left."
'Given:\n- Number of Siamese cats initially = 13\n- Number of house cats initially = 5\n- Total number of cats initially = 13 + 5 = 18\n- Number of cats sold during the sale = 10\n\nPlan:\n1. Calculate the total number of cats initially.\n2. Subtract the number of cats sold during the sale from the total number of cats initially to find out how many cats are left.\n\nCalculation:\nTotal number of cats initially = 13 + 5 = 18\nNumber of cats left = 18 - 10 = 8\n\nTherefore, the pet store has 8 cats left after selling 10 cats during the sale.'
"Variables:\n- Games bought from a friend: 2\n- Games bought at a garage sale: 2\n- Games that didn't work: 2\n\nPlan:\n1. Luke bought a total of 2 + 2 = 4 games.\n2. If 2 of the games didn't work, then Luke ended up with 4 - 2 = 2 good games.\n\nAnswer:\nLuke ended up with 2 good games."
'Variables:\nR = number of red apples ordered\nG = number of green apples ordered\nT = total number of apples ordered\nS = number of students who wanted fruit\n\nGiven:\nR = 42\nG = 7\nS = 9\n\nCalculations:\nT = R + G\nT = 42 + 7\nT = 49\n\nExtra apples = T - S\nExtra apples = 49 - 9\nExtra apples = 40\n\nAnswer:\nThe cafeteria ended up with 40 extra apples.'
'Given:\nNumber of tulips picked = 36\nNumber of roses picked = 37\nTotal number of flowers picked = 36 + 37 = 73\nNumber of flowers used = 70\n\nTo find:\nNumber of extra flowers picked = Total number of flowers picked - Number of flowers used\n\nCalculations:\nNumber of extra flowers picked = 73 - 70\nNumber of extra flowers picked = 3\n\nTherefore, Lana picked 3 extra flowers.'
"Let's denote the number of bad carrots as B.\n\nWe know that Carol picked 29 carrots and her mom picked 16 carrots, so the total number of carrots picked is 29 + 16 = 45.\n\nSince only 38 of the carrots were good, the number of bad carrots can be calculated as:\nB = Total number of carrots - Number of good carrots\nB = 45 - 38\nB = 7\n\nTherefore, Carol and her mom had 7 bad carrots."
'Variables:\nInitial amount of money = $16\nMoney received for birthday = $28\nMoney spent on a new game = $25\n\nPlan:\n1. Add the initial amount of money and the money received for his birthday.\n2. Subtract the money spent on the new game from the total amount.\n\nCalculation:\n1. Initial amount + Money received = $16 + $28 = $44\n2. Total amount - Money spent = $44 - $25 = $19\n\nTherefore, Roger has $19 now.'
'Variables:\nPictures taken at the zoo = 15\nPictures taken at the museum = 18\nPictures deleted = 31\n\nPlan:\n1. Calculate the total number of pictures taken by Megan.\n2. Subtract the number of pictures deleted to find out how many pictures she still has.\n\nCalculation:\nTotal pictures taken = 15 (zoo) + 18 (museum) = 33\nPictures remaining = 33 - 31 = 2\n\nTherefore, Megan still had 2 pictures from her vacation after deleting 31 pictures.'
'Let:\n- Number of pictures in the first coloring book = 23\n- Number of pictures in the second coloring book = 32\n- Total number of pictures colored after one week = 44\n\nTo find out how many pictures Rachel still has to color, we need to calculate the total number of pictures she has in both coloring books and then subtract the number of pictures she has already colored.\n\nTotal number of pictures = 23 + 32 = 55\n\nNumber of pictures still to color = Total number of pictures - Number of pictures colored\nNumber of pictures still to color = 55 - 44\nNumber of pictures still to color = 11\n\nTherefore, Rachel still has 11 pictures to color.'
'Given:\nShort sleeve shirts = 9\nLong sleeve shirts = 21\nTotal shirts to wash = 9 + 21 = 30\nShirts washed before school = 29\n\nTo find out how many shirts Ned did not wash, we can subtract the number of shirts washed from the total number of shirts:\nNot washed = Total shirts - Shirts washed\nNot washed = 30 - 29\nNot washed = 1\n\nTherefore, Ned did not wash 1 shirt before school.'
'Variables:\nShort sleeve shirts = 39\nLong sleeve shirts = 47\nTotal shirts = 39 + 47 = 86\nShirts washed before school = 20\n\nPlan:\nTo find out how many shirts Oliver did not wash, we need to subtract the number of shirts he washed from the total number of shirts.\n\nCalculation:\nTotal shirts - Shirts washed before school = Shirts not washed\n86 - 20 = 66\n\nAnswer:\nOliver did not wash 66 shirts before school.'

Calculate the number of pastries sold: total pastries baked - pastries taken back home\n\nCalculation:\n1. Total pastries baked = 4 cupcakes + 29 cookies = 4 + 29 = 33 pastries\n2. Pastries sold = Total pastries baked - Pastries taken back home = 33 - 24 = 9 pastries\n\nTherefore, Wendy sold 9 pastries at the school bake sale.'

Total tickets won = Tickets won playing 'whack a mole' + Tickets won playing 'skee ball'\nTotal tickets won = 32 + 25\nTotal tickets won = 57\n\n2. Calculate the total number of apples ordered: Total = R + G\n2. Calculate the total number of apples needed for the students: Needed = S\n3. Calculate the extra apples: Extra = Total - Needed\n\nCalculation:\n1. Total = 43 + 32 = 75\n2. Needed = 2\n3. Extra = 75 - 2 = 73\n\nAnswer:\nThe cafeteria ended up with 73 extra apples.'

"Variables:\nV = number of carrots Vanessa picked\nM = number of carrots Vanessa's mom picked\nG = total number of good carrots\nB = total number of bad carrots\n\nGiven:\nV = 17\nM = 14\nG = 24\n\nWe know that the total number of carrots picked is the sum of the good and bad carrots:\nV + M = G + B\n17 + 14 = 24 + B\n31 = 24 + B\nB = 31 - 24\nB = 7\n\nTherefore, Vanessa and her mom had 7 bad carrots."

Calculate the number of trips needed to pick up all the trays from the first table.\n2. Calculate the number of trips needed to pick up all the trays from the second table.\n3. Add the number of trips from step 1 and step 2 to find the total number of trips Roger will make.\n\nCalculation:\n1. Number of trips to pick up 10 trays from the first table: 10 trays / 4 trays per trip = 2.5 trips\n   Since Roger cannot make half a trip, he will need to make 3 trips to pick up all 10 trays from the first table.\n2. "Let's denote the number of pictures Isabel uploaded from her phone as P and the number of pictures she uploaded from her camera as C. \n\nGiven that P = 2 and C = 4, the total number of pictures Isabel uploaded is P + C = 2 + 4 = 6.\n\nIsabel wants to sort the pictures into 3 different albums with the same amount of pictures in each album. Let's denote the number of pictures in each album as A.\n\nSince Isabel uploaded a total of 6 pictures and wants to divide them into 3 albums with the same number of pictures in each album, the number of pictures in each album can be calculated as:\n\nA = Total number of pictures / Number of albums\nA = 6 / 3\nA = 2\n\nTherefore, Isabel should put 2 pictures in each album."

Total money earned per week: $3 + $3 = $6\n2. Weeks the money will last: $6 / $3 = 2 weeks\n\nAnswer:\nThe money will last Paul for 2 weeks.'

Divide the total number of cookies by the number of cookies in each bag to find out how many baggies she can make.\n\nCalculation:\n1. Total number of cookies = Number of chocolate chip cookies + Number of oatmeal cookies\nTotal number of cookies = 23 + 25\nTotal number of cookies = 48\n\n2. "Let's denote the number of pictures in each album as x. \n\nWendy uploaded a total of 22 + 2 = 24 pictures.\n\nSince she sorted the pictures into 4 different albums with the same amount of pics in each album, the total number of pictures must be divisible by 4.\n\nTherefore, x must be a multiple of 4.\n\nThe possible values for x are 4, 8, 12, 16, 20, and 24.\n\nSince x cannot be greater than 24 (the total number of pictures), the only possible value for x is 8.\n\nTherefore, there were 8 pictures in each of the albums."

Calculate the total number of hours needed to paint the remaining rooms.\n4. Find out how much longer it will take to paint the rest of the rooms.\n\nCalculation:\n1. Subtract the number of wilted flowers from the total number of flowers to find out how many usable flowers she has left.\n3. Calculate how many bouquets she can make with the usable flowers.\n\nCalculation:\n1. Total number of bouquets = Total number of flowers picked / Number of flowers in each bouquet\nTotal number of bouquets = 66 / 8 = 8.25 (Since we can't have a fraction of a bouquet, we will consider only the whole number part)\n\n2. Number of usable flowers = Total number of flowers picked - Number of wilted flowers\nNumber of usable flowers = 66 - 10 = 56\n\n3. Number of bouquets Isabel can make with usable flowers = Number of usable flowers / Number of flowers in each bouquet\nNumber of bouquets = 56 / 8 = 7\n\nAnswer:\nIsabel can still make 7 bouquets for her friend's wedding."
"Given:\nTotal pieces of candy received = 108\nPieces of candy eaten = 36\nPieces of candy in each pile = 9\n\nLet's calculate the total number of pieces of candy left after Sarah ate 36 pieces:\nTotal pieces of candy left = Total pieces of candy received - Pieces of candy eaten\nTotal pieces of candy left = 108 - 36\nTotal pieces of candy left = 72\n\nNow, let's calculate the number of piles Sarah can make:\nNumber of piles = Total pieces of candy left / Pieces of candy in each pile\nNumber of piles = 72 / 9\nNumber of piles = 8\n\nTherefore, Sarah can make 8 piles of candy with the remaining 72 pieces."

Calculate the number of folders needed to store the remaining files.\n\nCalculation:\n1. Total files left = Total files - Deleted files\nTotal files left = 80 - 31\nTotal files left = 49\n\n2. Number of folders = Total files left / Files in each folder\nNumber of folders = 49 / 7\nNumber of folders = 7\n\nTherefore, Nancy ended up with 7 folders.'

'Given:\n- Haley baked 20 cupcakes\n- Todd ate 11 cupcakes\n- Each package contains 3 cupcakes\n\nNumber of cupcakes left after Todd ate: 20 - 11 = 9 cupcakes\n\nNumber of packages that can be made: 9 / 3 = 3 packages\n\nTherefore, Haley can make 3 packages of cupcakes with the remaining cupcakes.'
'Variables:\nTotal number of puppies = 13\nNumber of puppies sold = 7\nNumber of puppies left = 13 - 7 = 6\nNumber of puppies in each cage = 2\n\nPlan:\n1. Calculate the number of puppies left after selling 7 puppies.\n2. Divide the number of puppies left by the number of puppies in each cage to find the number of cages used.\n\nCalculation:\n1. Number of puppies left = 13 - 7 = 6\n2. Number of cages used = 6 / 2 = 3\n\nTherefore, the pet store used 3 cages to house the remaining 6 puppies.'

'Variables:\n- Initial amount of money Kaleb had: $12\n- Amount spent on a new game: $8\n- Cost of each 2 dollar toy: $2\n\nPlan:\n1. Calculate how much money Kaleb has left after spending $8 on the new game.\n2. Divide the remaining money by the cost of each 2 dollar toy to find out how many toys he can buy.\n\nCalculation:\n1. Money left after spending $8 on the new game:\n$12 - $8 = $4\n\n2. Number of 2 dollar toys Kaleb can buy with $4:\n$4 / $2 = 2\n\nAnswer:\nKaleb can buy 2 two-dollar toys with the money he has left after spending $8 on the new game.'
'Variables:\nTotal seeds = 21\nSeeds planted in big garden = 12\nSeeds planted in each small garden = 3\nNumber of small gardens = ?\n\nPlan:\n1. Calculate the total number of seeds planted in small gardens.\n2. Find out how many small gardens Sarah has by dividing the total number of seeds planted in small gardens by the number of seeds planted in each small garden.\n\nCalculation:\n1. Total seeds planted in small gardens = Total seeds - Seeds planted in big garden\nTotal seeds planted in small gardens = 21 - 12\nTotal seeds planted in small gardens = 9\n\n2. Number of small gardens = Total seeds planted in small gardens / Seeds planted in each small garden\nNumber of small gardens = 9 / 3\nNumber of small gardens = 3\n\nAnswer:\nSarah has 3 small gardens.'
'Let x be the number of pictures in each of the 8 different albums.\n\nThe total number of pictures uploaded = 51\nNumber of pictures in the first album = 11\nNumber of pictures in the 8 different albums = 51 - 11 = 40\n\nSince the 40 pictures are divided into 8 different albums, the number of pictures in each album is x.\n\nTherefore, x = 40 / 8 = 5\n\nSo, there were 5 pictures in each of the 8 different albums.'

Calculate the number of people who showed up.\n2. Determine the number of tables needed by dividing the number of people who showed up by the number of people a table can hold.\n\nCalculation:\n1. Number of people who showed up = 24 - 10 = 14\n2. Number of tables needed = 14 / 7 = 2\n\nAnswer:\nThe company needs 2 tables for the 14 people who showed up at the luncheon."
"Variables:\nBianca's points = 45\nOther players' points = 6\nTotal points = 75\n\nLet x be the number of other players on Bianca's team.\n\nPlan:\n1. Bianca scored 45 points, so the total points scored by other players = 75 - 45 = 30.\n2. Each other player scored 6 points, so the number of other players can be calculated by dividing the total points scored by other players by the points scored by each player.\n\nCalculation:\nTotal points scored by other players = 30\nPoints scored by each player = 6\nNumber of other players = 30 / 6 = 5\n\nTherefore, there were 5 other players on Bianca's team. Adding Bianca, the total number of players on her team is 5 + 1 = 6."

'Given:\nTotal pieces of clothing = 60\nNumber of pieces in the first load = 40\n\nLet x be the number of pieces in each of the small loads.\n\nThe number of pieces in the small loads can be calculated as follows:\nTotal pieces of clothing - Number of pieces in the first load = Number of pieces in the small loads\n60 - 40 = 20\n\nSince the 20 pieces of clothing need to be split into 5 equal loads, we can divide 20 by 5 to find out how many pieces of clothing can go in each small load:\n20 / 5 = 4\n\nTherefore, each of the small loads can contain 4 pieces of clothing.'

Calculate the number of cupcakes left for packaging after Todd ate some.\n2. "Let's denote the number of pictures in the first album as x, and the number of pictures in the second album as y. \n\nWe know that:\nx + y = 41 (total number of pictures)\nx + 2y = 41 (number of pictures in the first album + number of pictures in the two other albums)\n\nSubtracting the first equation from the second equation, we get:\nx + 2y - (x + y) = 41 - 41\nx + 2y - x - y = 0\ny = 0\n\nTherefore, there are 0 pictures in the second album. \n\nNow, we can substitute y = 0 into the first equation to find x:\nx + 0 = 41\nx = 41\n\nSo, there are 41 pictures in the first album and 0 pictures in the second album."
